Rude business model? I was third in a line of seven customers, but was the ONLY customer singled out to pay first before they would even start making my sandwich. I watched them make sandwiches for two other customers in front of me as we waited to pay. Each customer, except me, was handed their sandwich as they paid. I waited in the same line, ordered from the same menu, but nobody paid any attention to my sandwich until AFTER I paid. Meanwhile, I stood I watched two more customers get served immediately as I was waiting for my sandwich.

I spoke to the asst. manager, and she said that was standard practice for a grilled sandwich. So, if you like being disrespected because you want a hot sandwich, it looks like Jersey Mike's is the place. Really, what kind of business model is that? Pay for hot sandwiches first? Beautiful area.  Lots to see.  Trails are defined.  Good area to hike, think, and observe nature.  You see a few people, but not a crowded trail.  The views are amazing.  It was nice hiking with my husband and dogs.  Take lots of water.  There are some trails that are pretty steep.  You will see birds, lizards, and bees. <review>(three stars for communication)

I was referred here by a business associate and liked their price. You have to drive a bit more maybe, but worth it.

The ladies here are nice, but they have RULES and if you don't like their RULES, then you're out.  This is what I was told when I signed up.  In fact, I inquired very gently on the walk through, in a calm voice, as to why a certain lock was required (I haven't had storage in five years) and I was told matter of factly (in a harsh tone) that if I didn't agree with the lock requirement, I was free to shop around and "let them know" if I was still interested.  I could tell she has had a lot of inquiries like this and was probably ready for a fight.  But, I wasn't trying to have a fight.  I wanted to know why I had to have a lock that you don't normally see.  I looked up the lock on Amazon and it was a buck less than theirs so I bought it here.

I have been selling for 25 years and I sell a very serious and complicated product called insurance. If my associates treated my customers like this, I would have a lot of coaching time with them as to how to enforce rules, but also speak in gentle tones and to outline the reason for such rules. After this encounter, I walked into the office to find on the wall three or four nice bullet points of the actual "whys" related to the lock.  I imagine had Liz simply said "there are a few reasons... x, y, and z" like the poster I would have been satisfied.  She would have seemed like she knew her product and service as well.  My trust level for her would have sky rocketed.  Now, I worry I'm always on the line, waiting to be kicked out.

Her other focus was that if I were to ever stay late past gate hours, "I would be locked in and have to call the cops" to get me out after which I would be asked to leave the storage unit as a customer.  Wow.  Ok.  I get it.  Homelessness in LA is serious.  No boarders.  But, again, coaching needed here.  I drove up in a 2019 Volvo and presented my platinum Amex. (with which I immediately set up auto-pay)  Probably not going to shack up at StorAmerica.  I saw by the looks of one tenant giving them gruff, that there are possibly folks here that may not live in standard housing.  That's ok and I'm sure it can be a drag to deal with all the time.  But, again, learn a bit about your customer before you assume he'll break all the rules in two minutes, ESPECIALLY if I was referred to you.  You could lose two good clients. You don't know how tight I am with your referral.

The price is fair, the place is very clean, and I feel like my things are safe.  After our first encounter, Liz and I were able to work together. The "free" truck is nice and I used it to my benefit.  I think Liz and Darlene mean well and care about their jobs and the space, but please... coaching!  Gentle.  Nice. Smile a lot.  You'll find your day will be less stressful.  Thank you.<//review><pictures>None< /pictures><resp>{'time': 1578767761564, 'text': 'Hello Charles, thank you for your feedback. <resp>None< /resp>< text>
I wish that I still loved this place.  Since Sui Mei sold it, the quality of the food has gone down hill substantially.  For the life of them, they CANNOT COOK CHICKEN. The chicken in every single dish I have had has been both tough AND flavorless.  Even the dipping sauces have lost flavor.  The Sweet Pepper sauce is now a lightly flavored sweet-tart, that makes Panda Express seem Michelin-star-worthy.  They killed the Southern Thai curry which was a revelation of flavors not often seen together. Even the salad rolls are now flavor-light and reminiscent of a bad airplane salad.   The Brain Food was one of my favorites - it had light and subtle flavor that pleasantly seasoned the kale, which can overwhelm a dish, while enhancing the sweet potato notes with spices and a little heat.  Now it is pretty much a bland sweet potato-kale casserole with all the flavor of a Sprouts freezer TV dinner.    I wish they had someone in their kitchen who knew what the food was supposed to taste like.  Unfortunately that's not what's happened.
While the former owner was a most unpleasant woman - I personally saw her scream and throw food at her staff, dress them down and humiliate them (on more than one occasion) and holler at customers who displeased her - she developed many incredibly delicious recipes. I only wish the new and very nice owners could have preserved her recipes and flavors better than they have.  I used to go there despite the owner and now I only go when I forget how disappointing the food is.  Alas...</text>

< Review>
I've been meaning to add a review for a long time now but I've always held back because I like to give restaurants an opportunity and know that they can have a bad day. But I've repeatedly had bad days now with Saffron.

Today, 4/19/19 at around 5:09pm, I decided to stop by to buy some tofu rolls and brought them home. I came to realize that the tofu is  gone bad, the veggies old, and the rice sheet broke apart as I grabbed one.

I believe in second chances but I've given Saffron too many. It's not the cozy family own placed anymore.

I will avoid going here going forward and just wanted to share my thoughts.</Review>

Christie Coats</user_name>
<pics>None</pics>< text>
I'm a thai food lover, and I love that this place is just up the street from work. They have a great quick lunch time menu. They can turn around a soup or chicken dish in just a few minutes but that doesn't translate to a stale or less than flavorful taste. While parking can sometimes be tricky, even at lunch, I've never not found a parking spot if I just drive around the block and off of India Street. The people here are always friendly, the smells and food inviting. I never mind spending my lunch here. If you're in a hurry, they do have food to go, just remember to a lot a minute or two to find parking.</text>
